So, the number of students who suggested adding mashed potatoes can be represented as ""x + 63"".

The total number of students who suggested either mashed potatoes or bacon is the sum of these two groups: x + (x + 63) = 457.

Simplifying this equation, we get: 2x + 63 = 457.

Subtracting 63 from both sides of the equation, we have: 2x = 457 - 63.

Calculating the right side of the equation, we get: 2x = 394.

Finally, dividing both sides by 2, we find: x = 197.

Therefore, the number of students who suggested bacon is 197.

Now, let's calculate the mouse's jump:
Mouse's jump = Frog's jump - 5 inches
Mouse's jump = (24 inches + 33 inches) - 5 inches

Finally, let's find out how much farther the mouse jumped than the grasshopper by calculating the difference between their jumps:
Difference = Mouse's jump - Grasshopper's jump
Difference = [(24 inches + 33 inches) - 5 inches] - 24 inches

Simplifying the calculations:
Frog's jump = <<24 + 33>>
Mouse's jump = <<(24 + 33) - 5>>
Difference = <<[(24 + 33) - 5] - 24>>

Calculating each step:
Frog's jump = <<57>>
Mouse's jump = <<52>>
Difference = <<28>>

Therefore, the mouse jumped 28 inches farther than the grasshopper.

Jake had 6 balloons and Allan had 2 balloons initially. Allan then bought 3 more balloons at the park. 

To find the difference, we subtract the number of balloons Allan had from the number of balloons Jake had.

 6 - 2 = << 6 - 2 = 4 >> 4 

Therefore, Jake had 4 more balloons than Allan in the park.

Number of chapters = 2
Number of pages in the first chapter = 60
Total number of pages in the book = 93

Let's denote the number of pages in the second chapter as ""x"".

We know that:
Number of pages in the first chapter + Number of pages in the second chapter = Total number of pages in the book

Therefore, we can write the equation:
60 + x = 93

To solve for ""x"", we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. We can do this by subtracting 60 from both sides:

60 + x - 60 = 93 - 60
x = 33

Hence, there are 33 pages in the second chapter.

"the grasshopper the frog and the mouse had a jumping contest . the grasshopper jumped 21 inches . the grasshopper jumped 25 inches farther than the frog and the mouse jumped 16 inches lesser than the frog . how much farther did the grasshopper jump than the mouse ?" ; "Let's break down the information given in the problem:

1. The grasshopper jumped 21 inches.
2. The grasshopper jumped 25 inches farther than the frog.
3. The mouse jumped 16 inches lesser than the frog.

To find out how much farther the grasshopper jumped than the mouse, we need to determine the distances jumped by both the frog and the mouse.

Let's represent the distance jumped by the frog as ""x"" inches. According to the second statement, the grasshopper jumped 25 inches farther than the frog, so its distance can be represented as ""x + 25"" inches.

According to the third statement, the mouse jumped 16 inches lesser than the frog, so its distance can be represented as ""x - 16"" inches.

Now we can calculate how much farther the grasshopper jumped than the mouse by subtracting their distances:

Distance jumped by grasshopper - Distance jumped by mouse
= (x + 25) - (x - 16)

Simplifying this expression:

= x + 25 - x + 16
= x - x + 25 + 16
= 41

Therefore, the grasshopper jumped 41 inches farther than the mouse.

Let's denote the number of hours Julia spent playing tag with 19 kids on Monday as \( x \) hours, and the number of hours she spent playing tag with 18 kids on Tuesday as \( y \) hours. We know that the total time she spent playing tag on both days is 38 hours. So, we can write the following equation:

\[ x + y = 38  t(1) \]

We also know that she played tag with 19 kids on Monday and 18 kids on Tuesday. We need to find the difference in the number of kids she played with on Monday and Tuesday. Let's denote this difference as \( z \). We can write another equation based on the number of kids she played with:

\[ 19 - 18 = z  t(2) \]

Now, we can solve these equations simultaneously to find the values of \( x \), \( y \), and \( z \).

From equation (1), we can express \( y \) in terms of \( x \):

\[ y = 38 - x \]

Substituting this into equation (2), we can solve for \( z \):

\[ 19 - 18 = 38 - x \]

Simplifying this equation, we get:

\[ x = 21 \]

Now that we know the value of \( x \), we can find the value of \( y \) using equation (1):

\[ y = 38 - x = 38 - 21 = 17 \]

Finally, we can find the difference in the number of kids she played with on Monday and Tuesday (\( z \)):

\[ z = 19 - 18 = 1 \]

To isolate x, we can multiply both sides of the equation by -1:

(-1)(-x) = (-1)(-9)

x = 9

Therefore, Bobby had eaten 9 pieces of candy at the start.

We want to find out how many action figures he added to the shelf.

Starting with what we know:

Jerry initially had 7 action figures, and then he added some more. After that, he removed 10 of the old ones. So, the total number of action figures on the shelf after adding some and removing 10 old ones is:

<<7 + tadded - 10>>

And we know that this total is now 8. So, we can write the equation:

7 + tadded - 10 = <<7 + tadded - 10 = 8>> 8

To find the number of action figures he added, we can rearrange the equation:

tadded = <<tadded = 8 - 7 + 10>> 8 - 7 + 10

Now, let's calculate this:

tadded = <<tadded = 8 - 7 + 10 = 1 + 10 = 11>> 8 - 7 + 10 = 1 + 10 = 11

So, Jerry added 11 action figures to the shelf.

"jerry had some action figures on a shelf in his room . later he added 2 more action figures to the shelf and removed 7 of the old ones . if there are 10 action figures on his shelf now how many action figures did he have initially on the shelf ?" ; "Let's break down the problem step by step.

1. Jerry initially had some action figures on his shelf.
2. He added 2 more action figures.
3. He also removed 7 of the old ones.
4. Now, there are 10 action figures on his shelf.

We need to find out how many action figures Jerry had initially.

Let's use algebraic reasoning with << symbols to represent the initial number of action figures.

Jerry's initial number of action figures + 2 (added) - 7 (removed) = 10 (current total)

So, we can express this as an equation:

>> Initial + 2 - 7 = 10 <<

Now, let's solve for Initial.

>> Initial - 5 = 10 <<

To isolate Initial, add 5 to both sides of the equation.

>> Initial = 10 + 5 <<

Now, calculate the value of Initial.

>> Initial = 15 $

So, Jerry initially had 15 action figures on his shelf.

"some campers went rowing in the morning while 7 campers went rowing in the afternoon . if a total of 60 campers went rowing that day how many campers went rowing in the morning ?" ; "Let's use algebra to solve this problem step by step. We can represent the number of campers who went rowing in the morning as ""M"" and the number of campers who went rowing in the afternoon as ""A.""

We are given two pieces of information:

1. Some campers went rowing in the morning.
2. 7 campers went rowing in the afternoon.

According to the problem, the total number of campers who went rowing that day is 60. So, we can write an equation based on this information:

M (campers in the morning) + A (campers in the afternoon) = 60

We also know that 7 campers went rowing in the afternoon:

A = 7

Now, we can substitute the value of A into the equation:

M + 7 = 60

Next, we want to solve for M (the number of campers who went rowing in the morning), so we need to isolate M on one side of the equation. We can do this by subtracting 7 from both sides of the equation:

M + 7 - 7 = 60 - 7

M = 53

So, there were 53 campers who went rowing in the morning.

"ed had 24 more marbles than doug . doug lost 27 of his marbles at the playground while ed found 9 more marbles . how many more marbles did ed have than doug then ?" ; "Let's break down the problem step by step:

1. **Initially:**
   Let's assume Doug had \(D\) marbles.
   Ed had \(D + 24\) marbles.

2. **After Doug lost 27 marbles:**
   Doug has \(D - 27\) marbles.
   Ed still has \(D + 24\) marbles.

3. **After Ed found 9 more marbles:**
   Doug still has \(D - 27\) marbles.
   Ed has \((D + 24) + 9 = D + 33\) marbles.

4. **Difference in the number of marbles Ed had more than Doug:**
   Ed had \((D + 33) - (D - 27)\) marbles more than Doug.

   Simplifying this expression:
   \[(D + 33) - (D - 27) = D + 33 - D + 27\]
   \[= 33 + 27\]

Now, to find out how many more pages of reading homework she had than biology homework, subtract the number of biology pages from the number of reading pages:

\(11 t pages (reading) - 8 t pages (biology) = 3\) pages.

The total number of emails he received in the day is given as 5. 

So, the equation representing this situation is:
\[ 4 + x = 5 \]

To find the value of \( x \), we can subtract 4 from both sides of the equation:
\[ x = 5 - 4 \]

Performing the subtraction:
\[ x = 1 \]

6 + 3 + temails in the evening = <<6 + 3 + temails in the evening = 10>> 10

Now, to find out how many emails Jack received in the evening, we can rearrange the equation as follows:

temails in the evening = <<temails in the evening = 10 - 6 - 3>> 10 - 6 - 3

Now, let's calculate the value on the right-hand side of the equation:

temails in the evening = <<temails in the evening = 10 - 6 - 3 = 1>> 10 - 6 - 3 = 1

So, Jack received 1 email in the evening. Now, to find out how many emails he received in the afternoon:

Jack received 3 emails in the afternoon.

The total number of emails Jack received in the day is the sum of the emails in the afternoon, morning, and evening:

3 (tafternoon) + 6 (tmorning) + E (tevening) = <<3 (tafternoon) + 6 (tmorning) + E (tevening) = 10 (ttotal)>> 10 (ttotal)

Now, we can solve for <<E>>:

3 + 6 + E = <<3 + 6 + E = 10>> 10

9 + E = <<9 + E = 10>> 10

E = <<E = 10 - 9>> 10 - 9

E = <<E = 1>> 1

So, Jack received 1 email in the evening.

"the grasshopper the frog and the mouse had a jumping contest . the grasshopper jumped 19 inches . the frog jumped 39 inches farther than the grasshopper and the mouse jumped 94 inches lesser than the frog . how far did the frog jump ?" ; "To find out how far the frog jumped, we need to add the distance the grasshopper jumped to the additional distance the frog jumped beyond the grasshopper's jump. Then, we subtract the distance the mouse jumped from the frog's total jump.

1. **Distance jumped by the frog beyond the grasshopper's jump:**
   Frog's jump - Grasshopper's jump = \( 39 \, tinches \)

2. **Total distance jumped by the frog:**
   Frog's jump = \( 19 \, tinches + 39 \, tinches = 58 \, tinches \)

3. **Distance jumped by the mouse lesser than the frog's jump:**
   Mouse's jump = \( 58 \, tinches - 94 \, tinches = -36 \, tinches \)

The frog jumped \( 58 \) inches.

1. The grasshopper jumped 24 inches.
2. The frog jumped 33 inches farther than the grasshopper.
3. The mouse jumped 5 inches lesser than the frog.

To find out how much farther the mouse jumped than the grasshopper, we need to calculate the difference in the distances they jumped.

First, let's find out how far the frog jumped:

 Frog's\,Jump = << Frog's\,Jump = Grasshopper's\,Jump + 33 >> Grasshopper's\,Jump + 33 

 Frog's\,Jump = << Frog's\,Jump = 24 + 33 = 57\,inches >> 24 + 33 = 57\,inches 

Now, let's find out how far the mouse jumped:

 Mouse's\,Jump = << Mouse's\,Jump = Frog's\,Jump - 5 >> Frog's\,Jump - 5 

 Mouse's\,Jump = << Mouse's\,Jump = 57 - 5 = 52\,inches >> 57 - 5 = 52\,inches 

To find out how much farther the mouse jumped than the grasshopper:

 Mouse's\,Jump\,Farther\,Than\,Grasshopper = << Mouse's\,Jump\,Farther\,Than\,Grasshopper = Mouse's\,Jump - Grasshopper's\,Jump >> Mouse's\,Jump - Grasshopper's\,Jump 

 Mouse's\,Jump\,Farther\,Than\,Grasshopper = << Mouse's\,Jump\,Farther\,Than\,Grasshopper = 52 - 24 = 28\,inches >> 52 - 24 = 28\,inches 

So, the mouse jumped 28 inches farther than the grasshopper.

\[ C = 728 \]

1. Danny found 63 bottle caps at the park.
2. He threw away 51 old ones.
3. After that, he had 33 bottle caps in his collection.

To find out how many bottle caps Danny had at first, we need to determine his initial collection before he found the 63 bottle caps at the park.

Initial collection + Found at the park - Threw away = Final collection

Let's represent this with equations:

Let C represent Danny's initial collection.

C + 63 (found at the park) - 51 (threw away) = 33 (final collection)

Now, we can solve for C:

C + 63 - 51 = 33

C + 12 = 33

Subtract 12 from both sides:

C = 33 - 12

C = 21

So, Danny initially had 21 bottle caps.

So, Brenda had x cookies, and her mother had x cookies.

Now, we know they had to throw away 17 cookies in total. This means:

Brenda threw away x cookies, and her mother threw away x cookies. So, together they threw away 2x cookies.

Now, we can set up an equation:

2x = 17

To solve for x, we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. We can do this by dividing both sides by 2:

2x/2 = 17/2

x = 8.5

So, each of them had 8.5 cookies before they had to throw away 17 cookies.

2. Calculate how many people one seat can hold: 
   Each seat can hold 15 people.

3. Calculate how many people can ride one ferris wheel at a time: 
   19 seats * 15 people per seat = 285 people per ferris wheel.

4. Calculate how many people can ride 20 ferris wheels at the same time: 
   20 ferris wheels * 285 people per ferris wheel = 5700 people.

So, 20 ferris wheels can hold a total of 5700 people at the same time.
#### 5700"
"the ferris wheel in paradise park has 18 seats . each seat can hold 15 people . if 10 seats are broken how many people can ride the ferris wheel at the same time ?" ; "First, let's calculate the total number of people the ferris wheel can hold when all 18 seats are operational. To do that, we'll multiply the number of seats (18) by the capacity of each seat (15).

 18 * 15 = << 18 * 15 = 270 >> 270 

So, when all 18 seats are working, the ferris wheel can hold 270 people.

Now, let's calculate how many people can ride the ferris wheel when 10 seats are broken. To do this, we'll subtract the number of broken seats (10) from the total capacity (270).

 270 - 10 = << 270 - 10 = 260 >> 260 

When 10 seats are broken, the ferris wheel can still hold 260 people.

#### 260"
